## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models reaction rate laws where dA/dt depends on concentration A and possibly time t. The rate of change of a chemical species is governed by rate laws that are typically power-law functions of concentration, but can also involve rational forms (enzyme kinetics), time-dependent rate constants, or combinations arising from reduction of multi-species systems.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, simple decomposition)
- Second-order: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular same-species reaction)
- nth-order: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Mixed order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (saturation kinetics, enzyme-catalyzed)
- Substrate inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (enzyme kinetics with inhibition)
- Time-dependent rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalytic reaction)
- Reversible reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * (c2 - A) (forward and reverse first-order)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional kinetics with constant source/sink)
- Cooperative kinetics (Hill): dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (cooperative binding/reaction)
- DamkÃ¶hler-type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (complex surface reaction kinetics)
- Combined time-concentration: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (fractal or anomalous kinetics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure power-law dependence on concentration (dA/dt ~ A^n) indicates an elementary reaction of order n
- Rational functions of A (polynomials in numerator/denominator) suggest enzyme kinetics or quasi-steady-state reduced mechanisms
- Explicit time dependence in rate laws suggests non-isothermal conditions, photochemical forcing, or anomalous/fractal kinetics
- Product terms A*(c-A) indicate autocatalytic or logistic growth where A catalyzes its own production from a finite pool
- Square root dependence (A^0.5) can arise from dissociation equilibria or radical chain mechanisms
- Negative constant terms alongside A-dependent terms suggest competing production and consumption (source-sink dynamics)
- Polynomial quotients with A in both numerator and denominator indicate Langmuir-Hinshelwood or Michaelis-Menten surface/enzyme mechanisms
- If dA/dt depends on t only through A(t), the system is autonomous and t should not appear explicitly in the rate law
